Large/generated file hazard review for future coding agents

Purpose

This second-pass audit marks files that are expensive or dangerous to misinterpret: large generated vendor chunks, stale bundle families, tiny compatibility wrappers, remote asset-diff snapshots, and big media. Do not patch these files by name alone.

High-risk conclusions

- `public/assets/vendor-supabase-DAiUAuun.js` is the real public Supabase vendor chunk in the active bundle graph. It contains Supabase client/auth/storage/realtime code and is referenced by current chunks.
- `public/assets/vendor-supabase-CdzVlbop.js` is only a 47-byte compatibility re-export wrapper to `vendor-supabase-DAiUAuun.js`; patching it will not patch Supabase behavior unless the stale wrapper path is what is loaded.
- `artifacts/asset-diff/remote-assets/vendor-supabase-CdzVlbop.js` has a `.js` name but starts with `<!doctype html>`; it is a remote/build fallback snapshot, not an executable Supabase vendor chunk.
- `public/assets/index-BPYJFSVW.js` is the current entry injected by `public/restore-and-launch.js`; `public/assets/index-qd2KF3Jd.js` is a large older/stale entry candidate that references wrapper chunks such as `vendor-supabase-CdzVlbop.js`.
- Several remote asset-diff files share names with active public assets but differ in SHA/size. Treat `artifacts/asset-diff/**` as comparison/reference material unless direct serving evidence proves otherwise.

Rules for future agents

- Never infer behavior from a hashed filename. Open the file and trace the active entry graph first.
- Before editing any `public/assets/vendor-*` file, check whether it is a real chunk, a wrapper, stale, or a comparison artifact.
- Do not edit minified/built chunks as the first choice. Prefer source files or server runtime patches unless the repo intentionally serves patched bundles.
- Do not treat `artifacts/asset-diff/remote-assets/**` as active runtime code. Compare hashes and references first.
- Large media/audio files dominate repo size but usually do not affect auth/sync logic.
- Tiny wrapper chunks with old hash names exist for compatibility; they can keep stale bundle graphs alive in browser caches.
- If sync/auth behavior is wrong, trace `server.mjs`, `public/auth-bridge.js`, `public/restore-and-launch.js`, active `index-BPYJFSVW.js`, active `App-pJGjDiPw.js`, and real `vendor-supabase-DAiUAuun.js` before touching stale chunks.
